Why Not Many Spheres?
Sanusi justifies rejection of excessive spheres.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical astronomers did not adopt the view that each fixed star has its own sphere, and the principle of avoiding unnecessary excess in celestial matters.

Core Idea
Celestial models avoid unnecessary spheres: no evidence, no need.

Sanusi opens the door to a theoretical possibility: each fixed star could have its own sphere, and non-planetary spheres could be many. Yet he immediately explains why the classical astronomers rejected this option. This lesson explores that reasoning, grounded in the absence of evidence and the principle of avoiding superfluity in the heavens.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on multiplicity
Read the Arabic and translation for the first part of the source, which states the permissibility of many spheres and the reasons for not adopting that view.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا قطع لجواز' — it indicates logical possibility, not certainty.
2
Identify the two reasons for rejection
The text gives two reasons: lack of evidence (عدم الدليل) and lack of need (لا حاجة إليه). Reflect on why these are sufficient for astronomers.
This reflects a methodological principle: do not multiply entities without necessity.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Ask yourself: how does this principle relate to the other views presented later in the full source? It sets a baseline for evaluating alternative sphere counts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في جانب الكثرة فلا قطع لجواز أن يكون كل من الثوابت على فلك وأن تكون الأفلاك غير الكوكبية كثيرة محيط بعضها بالبعض، لكنهم لم يذهبوا إلى ذلك لعدم الدليل ولأنهم لم يجدوا في السمويات فضلاً لا حاجة إليه، وجوز بعضهم أن تكون الأفلاك ثمانية تستند الحركة الأولى إلى مجموعها، لا إلى فلك خاص وذلك بأن تتصل بها نفس واحدة تحركها الحركة اليومية. قال صاحب التحفة: فيجوز أن تكون سبعة بأن تكون الثوابت ودوائر البروج على محدب فلك زحل، وتتعلق نفس بمجموع السبعة تحركها الحركة الأولى، وأخرى بالسابعة تحركها الحركة الأخرى، لكن بشرط أن نفرض دوائر البروج متحركة بالسريعة دون البطيئة لتنتقل الثوابت بها من برج إلى برج كما هو الواقع.
As for the side of multiplicity, there is no certainty regarding the permissibility that each of the fixed stars be on a sphere and that the non-planetary spheres be many, each surrounding another. However, they did not adopt that due to lack of evidence and because they found no excess in celestial matters that is not needed. And some allowed that the spheres be eight, attributing the first motion to their totality, not to a specific sphere, by a single soul attached to them moving them with the daily motion. The author of al-Tuhfah said: 'It is permissible that they be seven, by having the fixed stars and the zodiac circles on the convex surface of the sphere of Saturn, and a soul attaches to the seven as a whole moving them with the first motion, and another to the seventh moving it with the other motion, but on condition that we assume the zodiac circles move with the fast motion and not the slow, so that the fixed stars are transferred by them from sign to sign, as is actually the case.'
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether there could be more or fewer than nine spheres. The author first notes that regarding multiplicity, there is no definitive judgment: it is possible that each fixed star has its own sphere, and that there are many non-planetary spheres surrounding one another. However, the classical astronomers did not adopt this view because they had no evidence for it, and they found no excess in the heavens that was unnecessary. The author then mentions that some allowed an eight-sphere system, where the first motion is attributed to the entire set of eight rather than to a separate ninth sphere, with one soul moving them all. Then the author quotes 'the author of al-Tuhfah' who suggests a seven-sphere system: the fixed stars and zodiac circles are placed on the convex surface of Saturn's sphere, with one soul moving the entire set (seven spheres) with the first motion, and another soul moving the seventh sphere (presumably the sphere of the moon or planets?) with the second motion. The condition is that the zodiac circles move with the fast motion (daily) and not the slow, so that the fixed stars are carried from sign to sign as observed. This shows the flexibility of the system while adhering to observed phenomena.

Key Terms
الثوابت
الأفلاك غير الكوكبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the classical astronomers randomly multiplied spheres without reason.
Correction: They only added spheres when necessary; they rejected unnecessary complexity.

Checkpoint
Why did the classical astronomers not adopt the view that each fixed star has its own sphere?
A) Because they considered it logically impossible.
B) Because of lack of evidence and lack of need.
C) Because the fixed stars are not actually stars.
D) Because they preferred the eight-sphere system.

Key Takeaway
Classical astronomers avoided multiplying spheres without evidence or necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever added practices or beliefs to your faith that have no clear evidence from the Quran or Sunnah? What would it take for you to let them go, even if they feel meaningful?
?
The astronomers avoided excess in celestial matters because 'they found no need.' Where in your daily life do you find yourself adding unnecessary complexity — in worship, relationships, or self-expectations? Can you name one thing you can simplify today to be more aligned with divine guidance?
?
If you truly believed that God does not create or command without purpose, how would that change the way you approach your own habits and beliefs? What is one unexamined assumption you are holding onto that you now feel accountable to investigate?

When Fewer Spheres Suffice: Eight or Seven?
Sanusi presents alternative sphere-counts (eight and seven) and their justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative proposals for eight-sphere and seven-sphere celestial systems, and the condition needed for the seven-sphere model to work.

Core Idea
Some scholars allowed fewer spheres—eight or seven—by redistributing motions.

After noting that excessive spheres are unnecessary, Sanusi presents alternative views that reduce the number of spheres. Some allowed eight spheres, attributing the first motion to the whole set rather than a separate ninth sphere. Then he quotes the author of al-Tuhfah, who proposed a seven-sphere system with a clever condition. This lesson unpacks those proposals.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative proposals
Read the Arabic and translation for the part starting from 'وجوز بعضهم' to the end. Note the two different numbers: eight and seven.
2
Understand the eight-sphere model
In the eight-sphere model, the first motion (daily rotation) is attributed to the totality of the eight spheres, moved by a single soul, not to a separate ninth sphere.
This eliminates the need for a ninth sphere.
3
Analyze the seven-sphere model
The author of al-Tuhfah proposes placing fixed stars and zodiac circles on the convex surface of Saturn's sphere, with one soul moving all seven with the first motion and another moving the seventh (or innermost) with the other motion.
The condition: zodiac circles must move with the fast (daily) motion, not the slow, so fixed stars transit between signs as observed.
4
Reflect on the principle of necessity
These models show that the number of spheres is not fixed by revelation but can be minimized based on evidence and necessity.
This connects to the earlier lesson: avoid unnecessary excess.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في جانب الكثرة فلا قطع لجواز أن يكون كل من الثوابت على فلك وأن تكون الأفلاك غير الكوكبية كثيرة محيط بعضها بالبعض، لكنهم لم يذهبوا إلى ذلك لعدم الدليل ولأنهم لم يجدوا في السمويات فضلاً لا حاجة إليه، وجوز بعضهم أن تكون الأفلاك ثمانية تستند الحركة الأولى إلى مجموعها، لا إلى فلك خاص وذلك بأن تتصل بها نفس واحدة تحركها الحركة اليومية. قال صاحب التحفة: فيجوز أن تكون سبعة بأن تكون الثوابت ودوائر البروج على محدب فلك زحل، وتتعلق نفس بمجموع السبعة تحركها الحركة الأولى، وأخرى بالسابعة تحركها الحركة الأخرى، لكن بشرط أن نفرض دوائر البروج متحركة بالسريعة دون البطيئة لتنتقل الثوابت بها من برج إلى برج كما هو الواقع.
As for the side of multiplicity, there is no certainty regarding the permissibility that each of the fixed stars be on a sphere and that the non-planetary spheres be many, each surrounding another. However, they did not adopt that due to lack of evidence and because they found no excess in celestial matters that is not needed. Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether there could be more or fewer than nine spheres. The author first notes that regarding multiplicity, there is no definitive judgment: it is possible that each fixed star has its own sphere, and that there are many non-planetary spheres surrounding one another. However, the classical astronomers did not adopt this view because they had no evidence for it, and they found no excess in the heavens that was unnecessary. What condition did the author of al-Tuhfah set for his seven-sphere model to work?
A) The zodiac circles must move with the slow motion.
B) The fixed stars must be on separate spheres.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Equatorial Circle, Poles, and Daily Rotation
The author defines the equatorial circle, the poles, and the period of the daily rotation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of the equatorial circle, the celestial poles, and the period of the daily rotation as explained in this cosmological model.

Core Idea
The celestial equator and poles define the framework of the daily rotation.

In this passage, the author clarifies key astronomical concepts foundational to understanding the daily motion of the heavens. He defines the 'zone' (mintaqah) as the great circle of rotation, its poles, and the circles parallel to it. He also explains the precise duration of one rotation—approximately a day and a night—with a slight adjustment due to the sun's own motion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main definitions
Read the passage carefully and list what is being defined: the equinoctial circle (muaddil al-nahar), the poles, and the small circles parallel to the zone.
Notice the Arabic technical terms for each.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is it called 'equinoctial'? Why does the author say 'about' a day and a night? The passage provides the reasons.
The sun's proper motion causes the day to be slightly longer than the rotation.
3
Connect the concepts
How do the equator, poles, and orbits relate to the daily motion? The great circle is produced by rotation, the poles are fixed points, and the small circles are parallel orbits.
This framework is essential for later discussions on celestial motions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدوائر الموازية للمنطقة تسمى مدارات تلك الحركة. قال (يسمى معدل النهار) وقطبين يسميان قطبي العالم. لتعادل الليل والنهار في جميع البقاع عند كون الشمس عليها، والمراد بالمنطقة أعظم الدوائر الحادثة من حركة الكرة على نفسها وبقطبيها النقطتان الثابتتان عند حركة الكرة، والدوائر الصغار الموازية للمنطقة تسمى مدارات تلك الحركة، وأحد قطبي العالم وهو الذي يلي شمال المواجه للمشرق ويسمى الشمالي والآخر الجنوبي. قال ويتم دورة في قريب من اليوم بليلة. إنما قال في قريب لأنها تنقص من اليوم بليلته بمقدار الحركة الخاصة للشمس من المغرب إلى المشرق.
The circles parallel to the zone (al-mintaqah) are called the orbits of that motion. He said: 'It is called the equinoctial circle (mu‛addil al-nahār),' and two poles are called the poles of the world. Because of the equality of night and day in all regions when the sun is upon it. What is meant by 'the zone' is the greatest circle produced by the rotation of the sphere on itself, and by 'its two poles' are meant the two fixed points during the rotation of the sphere. The small circles parallel to the zone are called the orbits of that motion. One of the poles of the world is the one that faces north, opposite to the east, and is called the northern pole, and the other is the southern. He said: 'It completes a rotation in about a day and a night.' He only said 'about' because it falls short of a day and a night by the amount of the sun's proper motion from west to east.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage defines key celestial circles and points related to the daily motion of the ninth sphere. It begins by stating that the circles parallel to the 'zone' (mintaqah, the celestial equator) are called orbits of that motion. The text then quotes the base text: 'It is called the equinoctial circle' (mu‛addil al-nahār) because when the sun is on it, day and night are equal everywhere. The 'zone' is defined as the great circle produced by the sphere's rotation on itself, and its poles are the fixed points during rotation. The smaller parallel circles are also orbits. The two poles are named: the one facing north (in the direction of the east?) is the northern pole, and the other is the southern. Finally, the author explains the period of the daily rotation: it completes a rotation in about a day and a night. The qualification 'about' is because the rotation is slightly shorter than a full solar day due to the sun's own slow westward-to-eastward motion (the sun's annual motion), which causes the day to be longer than the actual rotation period.

Key Terms
معدل النهار
قطبا العالم
المنطقة
الدوائر الموازية
الحركة اليومية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the equatorial circle (muaddil al-nahar) is the same as the ecliptic or the zodiacal band.
Correction: The text distinguishes the 'zone' (mintaqah) as the great circle of rotation, which is the equatorial circle, not the ecliptic.

Checkpoint
Why is the equinoctial circle called 'muaddil al-nahar'?
A) Because it moderates the length of night.
B) Because when the sun is on it, day and night are equal everywhere.
C) Because it determines the seasons.
D) Because it is the circle of the fixed stars.

Key Takeaway
The daily rotation is defined by the celestial equator and poles, and its period is slightly less than a solar day due to the sun's own motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The daily rotation is not perfectly aligned with the solar day; there is a small gap caused by the sun's own motion. In what area of your life is there a similar 'gap'—a small but persistent drift away from the straight path? What specific 'proper motion' is pulling you, and how can you recalibrate to align with Allah's order?
?
The celestial equator is where day and night are in perfect balance. But your life is likely filled with imbalance. Which domain—your spiritual duties, your family, your work—is most out of balance right now? What one practical step will you take today to restore equilibrium?
?
The poles remain fixed while the sphere rotates. Has anything in your life become an unmoving anchor of stability? Or are you constantly shifting with every wind? How can you make your commitment to Allah the unchanging pole of your existence?

This passage presents a key doctrine: the ninth sphere imparts motion to all spheres beneath it. This is based on observed celestial motion, particularly the daily rotation.

The Sphere of Fixed Stars: Motion and Periods
Al-Taftazani describes the sphere of fixed stars and enumerates three opinions on its rotation period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the location of the sphere of fixed stars, its direction of motion, and the differing scholarly opinions on its rotation period.

Core Idea
The fixed stars drift slowly westward over tens of thousands of years.

In this passage, al-Taftazani describes the sphere of fixed stars, the eighth sphere in the Ptolemaic model. He explains that it moves from west to east on its own ecliptic, distinct from the ninth sphere, and completes a full cycle in a period that scholars have estimated differently. The three main estimates are 36,000, 23,760, and 25,200 years, reflecting the uncertainty of pre-Islamic astronomy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: location, motion, period.
2
Identify the three rotation periods
The passage lists three numbers. Find them and write them down.
These are given in the Arabic as numbers: 36,000; 23,760; 25,200.
3
Reflect on the term 'fixed'
Consider why this sphere is called 'fixed' despite having motion. The commentary provides insight.
The stars appear fixed relative to each other, but the entire sphere moves slowly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلك الثوابت تحت الفلك التاسع قال (وتحته فلك الثوابت يتحرك من المغرب إلى المشرق على منطقة وقطبين غير منطقة التاسع، وقطبية ويتم دورة في ستة وثلاثين ألف سنة، أو في ثلاث وعشرين ألف سنة، وسبعمائة وستين سنة، أو في خمسة وعشرين ألف سنة، ومائتي سنة، على اختلاف الآراء)
The sphere of the fixed stars is under the ninth sphere. Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage defines the sphere of fixed stars (falk al-thawabit) as located under the ninth sphere. The commentator quotes the original text: beneath the ninth sphere lies the sphere of the fixed stars. This sphere moves from west to east on its own ecliptic (region) and poles, which are different from those of the ninth sphere. It completes one full precessional cycle in a period that is disputed: some say 36,000 years, others 23,760 years, and others 25,200 years. The passage simply states these differing opinions without adopting one.

The Order of Planets and the Naming of Fixed Stars
Al-Taftazani lists the seven planets and explains the term 'fixed stars'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Islamic order of planetary spheres and the two reasons why stars other than the seven planets are called 'fixed'.

Core Idea
Fixed stars move very slowly; their motion is only detected by precise observation.

This passage from Al-Taftazani describes the arrangement of the celestial spheres beneath the sphere of fixed stars and explains why most stars are called 'fixed.' Understanding this nomenclature clarifies an important concept in pre-modern astronomy: the distinction between the wandering planets and the apparently fixed stars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the list of planets and the explanatory remarks about the term 'fixed'.
2
Identify the planetary order
Find the sequence of planets listed: Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Sun, Venus, Mercury, Moon. Note the comment about the Sun's placement being 'by preference'.
This order reflects the Ptolemaic geocentric model.
3
Understand the meaning of 'fixed'
Focus on the two reasons given for calling stars 'fixed': extremely slow motion and constant distances/latitudes.
The first reason implies motion is too slow to perceive without careful measurement.
4
Reflect on the classification
Consider how this distinction between fixed stars and wandering planets fits into the broader cosmology of concentric spheres.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تحته فلك زحل، ثم المشتري، ثم المريخ، ثم الشمس، ثم زهرة، ثم عطارد، ثم القمر، استحساناً فيما بين الشمس والسفليين]. سمي بذلك لكونه مكاناً للكواكب الثوابت أعني ما عدا السبعة السيارة، وتسميتها ثوابت، إما لبطء حركتها في الغاية بحيث لم تدرك إلا بالنظر الدقيق، وإما لثبات ما بينها من الأبعاد على وتيرة واحدة وثبات عروضها عن منطقة حركتها
Then beneath it is the sphere of Saturn, then Jupiter, then Mars, then the Sun, then Venus, then Mercury, then the Moon, by preference regarding the Sun and the lower ones. It is named thus because it is a place for the fixed stars, meaning other than the seven wandering planets. And they are called fixed, either due to the extreme slowness of their motion such that it is not perceived except by precise observation, or due to the constancy of the distances between them in a uniform manner and the constancy of their latitudes from the region of their motion.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage continues the quotation. After describing the sphere of fixed stars, the original text lists the spheres beneath it in order: Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Sun, Venus, Mercury, and the Moon, with the note that the arrangement of the Sun and the lower planets is by preference (i.e., not definitive). Then the commentator explains why this sphere is called 'the sphere of fixed stars': it contains the fixed stars, which are all stars except the seven wandering planets (the classical planets). The term 'fixed' (thawabit) is used either because their motion is extremely slow, detectable only by careful measurement, or because the distances between them remain constant, as well as their latitudes (distance from the ecliptic) remaining fixed.

The Motion of the Eighth Sphere and Planetary Classification
Al-Taftazani explains the motion of the eighth sphere and planetary classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eighth sphere's motion requires a distinct axis, the historical disagreement on its precession rate, and how planets are classified as wanderers and luminaries.

Core Idea
Precession rates reveal the complexity of celestial motion and the limits of ancient observation.

In this passage, al-Taftazani presents the astronomical reasoning behind the motion of the fixed stars. He explains why astronomers concluded that the eighth sphere moves on its own axis, describes the controversy over its speed, and ends with a quick classification of the planets. This lesson unpacks each component, showing how early Islamic astronomers reconciled observation with Ptolemaic theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice the logical argument about motions being indistinguishable if axes coincide.
2
Identify the three precession rates
Find the three different opinions on how many years it takes to cover one degree. Compare the cycle lengths (36,000; 23,760; 25,200 years).
This shows that even expert astronomers disagreed based on their instruments.
3
Understand the planetary classification
Notice the last part: the moon's sphere is below all, and the seven planets are divided into 'wanderers' (sayyara) and 'two luminaries' (nayyiran). The rest are called 'mutaḥayyira' (also wandering).
This classification is based on apparent motion relative to the fixed stars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكموا بكون حركة الثامن على منطقة وقطبين غير منطقة التاسع وقطبيه، لأن حركة الحاوي والمحوى إذا كانت على مناطق وأقطاب بأعيانها، لا تحس باختلاف الحركتين، بل إنما يحس بحركة واحدة هي مركبة من مجموعهما إن اتحدت الجهة ، أو حاصلة من فضل السريعة على البطيئة إن اختلفت الجهتان، وإلا لم يحس بالحركة أصلاً، بل يرى ساكناً. وأيضاً يعرف بآلات القياس أن الثوابت لا تختلف أبعادها عن قطبي العالم، بل عن نقطة غيرهما، واختلفوا في مقدار هذه الحركة فعلى رأي بطليموس ومن قبله تقطع في كل مائة سنة درجة، فتتم الدورة في ست وثلاثين ألف سنة، وعلى رأي المتأخرين تقطع في كل ست وستين سنة درجة، فتتم الدورة في ثلاثة وعشرين ألف سنة، وسبعمائة سنة، وستين وبعضهم وجدوها تقطع الدرجة في كل سبعين سنة، فتتم الدورة في خمسة وعشرين ألف سنة، ومائتي سنة ، ويوافقه رصد مراغة، فيمكن أن يكون ذلك لاختلال في الآلات، أو لأسباب لا يطلع عليها إلا خالق السموات. فلك القمر تحت كل الأفلاك قال واستدلالاً من الكسف) في البواقي والكواكب السبعة تسمى السيارة، والشمس والقمر يسمى النيرين والباقي المتحيرة ]
And they ruled that the motion of the eighth is on a region and two poles other than the region of the ninth and its poles, because the motion of the container and the contained, if they were on the same regions and poles, would not be perceived as two different motions; rather, only one motion would be perceived, which is compounded from both if the direction is the same, or resulting from the excess of the faster over the slower if the directions differ; otherwise, no motion would be perceived at all, but it would be seen as stationary. Also, it is known by measuring instruments that the fixed stars do not differ in their distances from the poles of the universe, but rather from a point other than them. And they differed concerning the amount of this motion: according to Ptolemy and those before him, it cuts one degree every hundred years, so the cycle is completed in thirty-six thousand years; according to the later ones, it cuts one degree every sixty-six years, so the cycle is completed in twenty-three thousand seven hundred sixty years; and some found it cuts one degree every seventy years, so the cycle is completed in twenty-five thousand two hundred years, and it agrees with the Maragha observatory. So it is possible that this is due to defects in the instruments, or for reasons that only the Creator of the heavens knows. The sphere of the moon is under all spheres. He said: And by deduction from the eclipses... among the rest, and the seven planets are called the wanderers, and the Sun and Moon are called the two luminaries, and the rest are the wandering ones.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses the motion of the eighth sphere (the sphere of fixed stars). The scholars ruled that it moves on its own ecliptic and poles, different from those of the ninth sphere. The reason given is that if two nested spheres moved on the same axis, their motions would not be perceived separately; either a combined motion or no motion would be observed. Instruments confirm that the fixed stars maintain constant distances from the celestial poles but vary from another point, indicating a separate axis. There is disagreement on the precession rate: Ptolemy and ancients said 1 degree per century (36,000-year cycle); later astronomers said 1 degree per 66 years (23,760 years); and some found 1 degree per 70 years (25,200 years), which matches the Maragha observatory. Inaccuracies might be due to instrument errors or unknown causes. Then the passage states that the sphere of the moon is under all spheres, and mentions that by deduction from eclipses, the seven planets are called 'wandering' (sayyara), while the Sun and Moon are called the 'two luminaries' (nayyiran), and the remaining planets are also wandering. This classification is standard.

Key Terms
حركة الثامن
بطليموس
رصد مراغة
نيرين
سيارة
متحيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is only one correct precession rate agreed upon by all astronomers.
Correction: Al-Taftazani explicitly records multiple rates from different authorities, including Ptolemy, later scholars, and the Maragha observatory, showing legitimate disagreement.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The precession of the eighth sphere illustrates how astronomers used observations and reasoning to determine the structure of the heavens, while also acknowledging uncertainty in measurements.

The Fixed Stars' Motion and Disagreement on Its Period
Discussion of motion perception and precession rates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how astronomers historically disagreed on the period of the fixed stars' precession and how the perception of motion can be affected by the combination of multiple motions.

Core Idea
The fixed stars move, but how fast? Astronomers disagreed, and perception can deceive.

In this passage, the author explains a key principle about how we perceive combined motions—two motions can sum, subtract, or cancel perceptually. Then he turns to the fixed stars, noting that instruments confirm they move, but the rate is uncertain: Ptolemy, later scholars, and the Maragha observatory each gave different values. This introduces both a philosophical insight about perception and a historical note on astronomical disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the shift from the general principle of motion perception to the specific case of fixed stars.
2
Understand the perceptual combination rule
The passage states that if two motions have the same direction, the perceived motion is their sum; if opposite, it's the difference; otherwise, no motion is perceived. This is a key concept for understanding how we observe celestial motions.
Ask yourself: what would happen if the two motions are equal and opposite?
3
Identify the three opinions on precession period
The passage lists three different values: Ptolemy's 36,000 years, later scholars' 23,760 years, and another of 25,200 years supported by Maragha observatory. Note the exact numbers.
4
Reflect on the reason for disagreement
The author suggests the discrepancy may be due to instrumental error or hidden causes known only to Allah. Consider the humility required in empirical science.
This shows that even in classical astronomy, uncertainty was acknowledged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باختلاف الحركتين، بل إنما يحس بحركة واحدة هي مركبة من مجموعهما إن اتحدت الجهة ، أو حاصلة من فضل السريعة على البطيئة إن اختلفت الجهتان، وإلا لم يحس بالحركة أصلاً، بل يرى ساكناً. وأيضاً يعرف بآلات القياس أن الثوابت لا تختلف أبعادها عن قطبي العالم، بل عن نقطة غيرهما، واختلفوا في مقدار هذه الحركة فعلى رأي بطليموس (۱) ومن قبله تقطع في كل مائة سنة درجة، فتتم الدورة في ست وثلاثين ألف سنة، وعلى رأي المتأخرين تقطع في كل ست وستين سنة درجة، فتتم الدورة في ثلاثة وعشرين (٢) ألف سنة، وسبعمائة سنة، وستين وبعضهم وجدوها تقطع الدرجة في كل سبعين سنة، فتتم الدورة في خمسة وعشرين ألف سنة، ومائتي سنة، ويوافقه رصد مراغة (۳)، فيمكن أن يكون ذلك لاختلال في الآلات، أو لأسباب لا يطلع عليها إلا خالق السموات.
Due to the difference of the two motions; rather one only perceives a single motion that is composed of the sum of both if the direction is the same, or resulting from the excess of the faster over the slower if the directions differ, otherwise no motion is perceived at all, but it is seen as stationary. Also by instruments it is known that the fixed stars do not vary in their distances from the poles of the world, but from a point other than them, and they differed on the amount of this motion: according to Ptolemy (1) and those before him, it moves one degree every hundred years, so the cycle completes in 36,000 years; according to later scholars, it moves one degree every sixty-six years, so the cycle completes in 23,760 years; and some found it moves one degree every seventy years, so the cycle completes in 25,200 years, and the Maragha observatory (2) agrees with it. So it may be due to a fault in the instruments, or for reasons known only to the Creator of the heavens.

Commentary
This passage discusses the motion of the fixed stars (precession). It begins by explaining how motions combine perceptually: when two motions are in the same direction, the perceived motion is their sum; when opposite, the difference; otherwise, no motion is perceived. Then it states that instruments show the fixed stars change their positions relative to a point other than the poles, which implies they have a motion. The passage then presents three different opinions on the period of this motion: Ptolemy's 36,000 years, later scholars' 23,760 years, and another opinion of 25,200 years supported by the Maragha observatory. Proof that the Moon's Sphere is Below All from Lunar Eclipses
Argument from lunar eclipses for the order of spheres

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument and the aesthetic reasoning used to determine the order of celestial spheres, specifically why the moon's sphere is considered below all and why the sun's position above Venus and Mercury is based on fittingness rather than necessary proof.

Core Idea
Observations of eclipses place the moon's sphere below all others; the sun's position is a matter of beautiful order.

In this passage, the author presents an argument from astronomy that uses observable phenomena (eclipses) to determine the relative positions of celestial spheres. While the moon's position is established by direct evidence of it eclipsing other bodies, the sun's placement above Venus and Mercury is not proven with certainty but is instead argued from the aesthetic harmony of the system, comparing the sun to the central jewel of a necklace. This lesson walks you through the evidence and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the technical terms. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
The passage uses specialized astronomical terms like 'الكسف' (eclipse).
2
Identify the evidence for the moon's sphere
The author states that astronomers observed the moon eclipsing other planets and fixed stars. Therefore they judged its sphere to be below all. This is a direct observational proof.
3
Examine the reasoning for the sun's sphere
The sun is not eclipsed by any planet except the moon, and its brightness prevents observation of its eclipses. So its position above Venus and Mercury is not proven by observation but by 'istihsan' (aesthetic judgment) for the sake of orderly arrangement.
This is a weaker form of argument compared to the moon's case.
4
Appreciate the necklace analogy
The author compares the sun to the jewel in a necklace, placed in the middle among the wandering planets. This poetic analogy reinforces the aesthetic argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلك القمر تحت كل الأفلاك قال واستدلالاً من الكسف) في البواقي والكواكب السبعة تسمى السيارة، والشمس والقمر يسمى النيرين والباقي المتحيرة . يعني أنهم وجدوا القمر يكسف (۱) سائر السيارات، ومن الثوابت ما يكون على ممره، فحكموا بأن فلكه تحت الكل، وهكذا الحكم في البواقي إلا الشمس، فإنها لا يكسفها غير القمر ولا يدرك كسفها بشيء من الكواكب، لاحترافهـا عنـد مقارنتها، فالحكم بكونها فوق الزهرة وعطارد استحساناً لما فيه من حسن الترتيب، وجودة النظام، حيث يكون النير الأعظم في الوسط من السيارات بمنزلة شمسة القلادة، وقد تأكد هذا الاستحسان بمناسبات أخر.
The sphere of the moon is below all spheres. He said: And as an inference from the eclipse (al-kasf) of the rest, the seven planets are called the wanderers, and the sun and moon are called the two luminaries, and the rest are the perplexed. Meaning that they found that the moon eclipses all the other wanderers and some of the fixed stars that lie on its path, so they judged that its sphere is below everything. Likewise is the judgment for the rest except the sun, for it is not eclipsed by anyone other than the moon, nor is its eclipse perceived by any of the planets due to its brightness when they approach it. So the judgment that it is above Venus and Mercury is based on what is fitting, because of the good ordering and the excellence of the system, as the greatest luminary is in the middle of the wanderers like the jewel of a necklace. And this fittingness was confirmed by other coincidences.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents an astronomical argument based on observations of lunar eclipses of other planets. The author states that the moon's sphere is below all others because it covers (eclipses) other planets and some fixed stars. For the sun, it is never eclipsed by any planet except the moon, and its eclipse is not perceived by other bodies due to its brightness. Therefore, they place the sun above Venus and Mercury as a matter of aesthetic order, comparing the sun to a jewel in the center of a necklace. This placement is not based on rigorous proof but on what is fitting, supported by other coincidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The positions of all planets are proven with certainty from observations of eclipses.
Correction: While the moon's position is proven by eclipse observations, the sun's position above Venus and Mercury is not proven but argued from aesthetic order (istihsan).

Checkpoint
Why did astronomers judge that the moon's sphere is below all others?
A) Because the moon is smaller than other planets
B) Because the moon is observed to eclipse other planets and fixed stars
C) Because the moon moves faster than other planets
D) Because the moon does not shine by itself

Key Takeaway
The moon's sphere is below all because it eclipses them, but the sun's position above Venus and Mercury is based on aesthetic order, not empirical proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The moon's consistent eclipses gave scholars confidence in its position. What repeated patterns in your life have led you to strong convictions? Are you equally willing to test those convictions when counter-evidence appears, or do you cling to them because they 'fit' your worldview? Will you examine one assumption this week to see if it is based on proof or mere fittingness?
?
The sun's placement was accepted based on aesthetic harmony—like a jewel in a necklace. In your own decisions, do you prioritize what 'looks right' or 'feels harmonious' over what is rigorously evidenced? Could that lead you to embrace a beautiful but false order? Are you ready to disrupt your comfortable arrangement if truth demands it?
?
Some of your theological beliefs may rest on clear observation (like the moon's sphere), others on a sense of fittingness (like the sun's middle). Which of your convictions are certain, and which do you hold because they make the world seem orderly? Are you humble enough to admit the difference, and will you pray today for the courage to seek deeper proof where you have assumed too much?

Parallax and Planetary Order
Using parallax to determine planetary distances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how parallax is used to determine the relative distances of planets and why it could not be used for Venus and Mercury.

Core Idea
Parallax reveals closeness: the sun shows parallax, superior planets do not.

In this passage, the author presents a key astronomical argument using parallax to determine the order of planets. He defines parallax, applies it to the sun and superior planets, and explains why Venus and Mercury are excluded. This demonstrates the evidence-based reasoning in Islamic astronomy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with an anecdotal claim about Venus.
2
Understand the definition of parallax
The passage defines parallax as the distance between two lines from the planet to the zodiac. Understand that its presence indicates closeness, absence indicates distance.
Parallax is a key concept in astronomy.
3
Apply the logic to the sun and superior planets
Follow the reasoning: parallax is found for the sun but not for Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, or fixed stars, so the sun is below them. Then consider why Venus and Mercury are excluded.
The passage explains that these two are always near the sun, so parallax cannot be observed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم بعضهم أنه رأى الزهرة كشامة على صفحة الشمس، والحكم بكونها تحت الثلاثة العلوية . أعني زحل والمشتري والمريخ، مأخوذ من اختلاف المنظر، وهو بعد ما بين طرفي الخطين المارين بمركز الكوكب الواصلين إلى فلك البروج الخارج أحدهما من مركز العالم، والآخر موضع الناظر. فإن وجوده يدل على القرب منا، وعدمه على البعد ، وقد وجد للشمس دون العلوية والثوابت، فعلم أنها تحتها، ولم يعرف وجوده للزهرة وعطارد، لأنه إنما يعرف بإله لهم تسمى ذات الشعبتين تنصب في سطح نصف النهار ، والزهرة وعطارد لكونهما حوالي الشمس دائماً، لا يصلان إلى نصف النهار ظاهرين.
And some claimed that he saw Venus as a mole on the surface of the sun. And the judgment that it is below the three upper ones—I mean Saturn, Jupiter, and Mars—is taken from parallax, which is the distance between the two ends of the two lines passing through the center of the planet that reach the zodiac, one emerging from the center of the world and the other from the observer's position. For its existence indicates proximity to us, and its absence indicates distance. It has been found for the sun but not for the upper ones and the fixed stars, so it is known that it is below them. It was not known for Venus and Mercury because it is only known by an instrument they have called 'Dhāt al-Shu'batayn' that is set up on the meridian plane, and Venus and Mercury, because they are always near the sun, do not reach the meridian visible.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents two points. First, it mentions a claim that someone saw Venus as a spot on the sun (anecdotal). Second, it gives a formal argument using parallax to determine that the sun is below Saturn, Jupiter, and Mars. Parallax is defined as the apparent shift of a planet relative to the zodiac when viewed from the center of the world versus the observer. Its presence indicates the planet is closer; absence indicates farther. Parallax is observed for the sun but not for the three superior planets or fixed stars, so the sun is closer. For Venus and Mercury, parallax cannot be observed because they are always near the sun and cannot be seen on the meridian, so their position relative to the sun is inferred by other means.

الزهرة
عطارد
ذات الشعبتين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Parallax can be used for all planets to determine their distance.
Correction: Parallax is not observable for Venus and Mercury because they are always near the sun and do not reach the meridian, as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
Why was parallax not observed for Venus and Mercury?
A) They are too small
B) They are always near the sun and do not reach the meridian visibly
C) The instrument was not precise enough
D) They are transparent

Key Takeaway
Parallax observation shows the sun is closer than Saturn, Jupiter, and Mars, but cannot be used for Venus and Mercury due to their proximity to the sun.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The astronomers did not observe parallax for Venus and Mercury, but they did not conclude they were far; instead they recognized their own observational limitation. In what area of your life have you assumed the absence of evidence means the absence of truth? Will you pause today to consider that your vantage point might be limited?
?
A claim of seeing Venus as a spot on the sun was mentioned, but the passage relies on systematic evidence (parallax) to determine truth. When you hear an extraordinary claim, do you usually accept it emotionally or test it against consistent evidence? What claim are you currently believing without systematic verification?

Eccentric Sphere, Apogee, Perigee, and Complementing Bodies
Al-Taftazani defines the eccentric sphere and the complementing bodies that fill the gap.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the geometric relationship between the concentric and eccentric spheres, including the definitions of apogee, perigee, and the complementing bodies that fill the gap.

Core Idea
The eccentric sphere fits inside the concentric by touching at two points, with crescent-shaped fillers tapering in between.

This passage from Al-Taftazani's Sharh al-Maqasid explains a key concept in Ptolemaic astronomy: how an eccentric sphere (one whose center is not the Earth) can fit within a concentric sphere (centered on Earth). The solution involves two points of contact and two 'complementing bodies' that fill the remaining space. By the end, you'll see how these elements work together to model planetary motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to get an overall sense of the definitions.
Focus on the terms 'apogee' and 'perigee' as they appear.
2
Identify the two contact points
Locate where the passage describes the convex touch (apogee) and concave touch (perigee). Note that these are the only points where the two spheres meet.
3
Understand why complementing bodies are needed
Because the centers differ, there is a gap. The passage explains that two spherical bodies fill this gap, thick in the middle and tapering to the contact points.
These are not separate spheres but crescent-shaped fillers.
4
Analyze the alternating gradation
Notice how the thickness alternates: the outer complementing body is thinnest at apogee and thickest at perigee, while the inner is opposite. This ensures continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوافق المركز يماس بمحدبه محدب الموافق على نقطة واحدة هي أبعد نقطة عليه من مركز الأرض، ويسمى الأوج، وبمقعره مقعر الموافق على نقطة مقابلة أقرب نقطة عليه منه، ويسمى الحضيض، فبالضرورة يبقى الفضل للأولى، هي من موافق المركز بعد انفصال الخارج المركز عنه جسمين مستديرين على مركز العالم، غليظي الوسط بقدر ما بين مركزي الموافق المركز، والخارج المركز يستدق ذلك الغلظ إلى أن ينعدم عند نقطتي المتماس المقابلتين لغايتي الغلظ. وهذان الجسمان يسميان بالمتممين، ويكون ذلك التدرج من الغلظ إلى الرقة فيهما على التبادل، بمعنى أن غاية رقة الحاوي منهما يكون عند الأوج، وغاية غلظه عند الحضيض، وغاية رقة المحوى عند الحضيض، وغلظه عند الأوج.
The concentric [sphere] touches with its convexity the convex of the eccentric at a single point which is the farthest point on it from the center of the earth, and it is called the apogee; and with its concavity [it touches] the concave of the concentric at an opposite point, the nearest point on it from it, and it is called the perigee. So necessarily there remains a surplus for the first [sphere], which is from the concentric after the separation of the eccentric from it: two spherical bodies on the center of the world, thick at their middle as much as the distance between the centers of the concentric and the eccentric; that thickness tapers until it vanishes at the two points of contact opposite the two extremes of thickness. These two bodies are called the 'complementing bodies' (al-mutamimayn). And that gradation from thickness to thinness in them is alternatingly: meaning that the extreme thinness of the containing one of them is at the apogee, and its extreme thickness at the perigee; and the extreme thinness of the contained one is at the perigee, and its thickness at the apogee.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines several key terms in Ptolemaic astronomy. It begins by describing the relationship between a concentric sphere (الموافق المركز) and an eccentric sphere (الخارج المركز). The concentric sphere touches the eccentric at a single point on its convex side, which is the farthest point from the center of the earth, called the apogee (الأوج). On the opposite side, the concave surface of the concentric touches the eccentric at the nearest point, called the perigee (الحضيض). Because the eccentric sphere has a different center from the concentric, there is a gap between them that is filled by two spherical bodies called the complementing bodies (المتممين). These bodies are thickest at the middle of the gap, gradually tapering until they vanish at the points of contact. The gradation is alternating: the containing (outer) complementing body is thinnest at the apogee and thickest at the perigee, while the contained (inner) is thinnest at the perigee and thickest at the apogee. This explains how the eccentric sphere fits within the concentric sphere while maintaining continuity.

Key Terms
الأوج
الحضيض
الموافق المركز
الخارج المركز
المتممين
غاية الرقة
غاية الغلظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the complementing bodies are separate spheres that independently rotate.
Correction: They are actually crescent-shaped fillings that taper to zero thickness at the contact points and are part of the continuous solid medium.

Checkpoint
What are the two points called where the concentric and eccentric spheres touch?
A) Apogee and perigee
B) Zenith and nadir
C) Equator and ecliptic
D) Solstice and equinox

Key Takeaway
The eccentric sphere's position is defined by two contact points, and the resulting gap is filled by two complementing bodies that taper from thick to thin at opposite ends.

Definition of the Epicycle and Its Key Components
Al-Taftazani defines the epicycle and its properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of an epicycle, its contact points (apex and perigee), and why it is considered solid.

Core Idea
The epicycle is a solid sphere within an eccentric, touching at two points and carrying the planet.

Al-Taftazani begins by defining the epicycle, a crucial concept in Ptolemaic astronomy. Understanding its structure—the apex, perigee, and solid nature—is essential before moving to the planetary models. This lesson unpacks that definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the epicycle
Read the Arabic definition of the epicycle (التدوير) and its translation carefully. Notice the precise language used to describe its shape and contact points.
The epicycle is a sphere (كرة) within the thickness of an eccentric sphere.
2
Identify the apex and perigee
The text mentions two points: الذروة (apex) where the epicycle touches the convex of the eccentric, and الحضيض (perigee) where it touches the concave. Take note of these terms.
These are opposite points marking the highest and lowest positions of the epicycle relative to the eccentric.
3
Understand why the epicycle is considered solid
The text says 'ولم يعتبر لها ولا للكوكب تقعير بل اعتبرا مصمتين' – they are considered solid, not hollow. This is important for the mechanics.
This means the epicycle and the planet are treated as solid bodies with no interior concavity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يكون الخارج المركز في ثخن خارج مركز آخر كما في عطارد ومنها التداوير، والتدوير كرة في ثخن الخارج المركز، يماس سطحها محدب الخارج بنقطة يسمى الذروة ومقعره بنقطة مقابلة لها تسمى الحضيض، والكوكب مركوز فيهما بحيث يتماس سطحاهما على نقطة ولم يعتبر لها ولا للكوكب تقعير بل اعتبرا مصمتين فقوله، ثم في ثخن المائل إشارة إلى أن الموافق المركز المشتمل على الخارج المركز هو في القمر المائل، وفي البواقي ممثلاتها، وأن الحامل اسم للخارج المركز إذا كان في ثخنه التدوير لحمله مركز التدوير، وإن خارج المركز مديراً لإدارته مركز الحامل، وهو الخارج المركز الذي ينفصل عن المدير انفصال المدير عن الممثل، ويكون فيه التدوير لعطارد خارجاً مركز وأوجان، وحضيضان وأربع متممات والمائل في المتحيرة اسم للخارج المركز الحامل للتدوير إذا تقرر هذا فنقول للشمس ممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز في ثخنه الشمس، وللقمر ممثل في جوفه مائل في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه القمر ولعطارد وممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز يسمى مديراً في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه عطارد، ولكل من الأربع الباقية ممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه الكوكب.
And the eccentric may be in the thickness of another eccentric, as in Mercury. And from these are the epicycles (al-tadawir). And the epicycle is a sphere in the thickness of the eccentric; its surface touches the convex of the eccentric at a point called the apex (al-dharwa) and its concave at an opposite point called the perigee (al-hadid). And the planet is fixed in both such that their two surfaces touch at a point, and concavity is not considered for them nor for the planet, but they are considered solid. So his statement: 'then in the thickness of the inclined [sphere]' indicates that the concentric containing the eccentric is in the inclined [sphere] of the moon, and in the rest, their representatives (mumaththilat). And that 'al-hamil' (the carrier) is the name for the eccentric if there is in its thickness an epicycle, because it carries the center of the epicycle. And that the eccentric is a 'mudir' (director) because its center is directed by the carrier. And it is the eccentric that is separate from the director as the director is separate from the representative. And in it, the epicycle for Mercury has an eccentric and two apogees and two perigees and four complementing bodies. And 'al-mail' (the inclined) in the wandering planets is the name for the eccentric that carries the epicycle. If this is established, then we say: For the Sun, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric in whose thickness is the Sun. For the Moon, there is a representative in its interior an inclined [sphere] in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is the Moon. For Mercury, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric called a director (mudir) in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is Mercury. And for each of the remaining four, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is the planet.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage continues the astronomical discussion by introducing the epicycle (التدوير) and detailing the models for each planet. It begins by noting that an eccentric can be nested within another eccentric, as for Mercury. From such configurations come epicycles, defined as a sphere within the thickness of an eccentric, touching it at two points: the apex (الذروة) and the perigee (الحضيض). The planet is fixed on the epicycle such that the surfaces touch at a point, and both the epicycle and planet are considered solid (not hollow). The text then explains terminology: the 'carrier' (الحامل) is the eccentric that contains an epicycle; the 'director' (المدير) is an eccentric that is separate from the carrier; the 'representative' (الممثل) is a sphere that contains these. For the Moon, the concentric containing the eccentric is in an inclined sphere; for other planets, they have representatives. Mercury's model has an eccentric, two apogees, two perigees, and four complementing bodies. The 'inclined' (المائل) in the wandering planets is the eccentric that carries the epicycle. Finally, it summarizes each planet: Sun has a representative with an eccentric containing the Sun; Moon has a representative with an inclined sphere containing an eccentric carrier; Mercury has a representative with an eccentric director containing an eccentric carrier; the other four planets each have a representative with an eccentric carrier. This establishes the complex layering of spheres used to explain planetary motions.

Key Terms
التداوير
التدوير
الذروة
الحضيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the epicycle is the planet's orbit; actually the planet is fixed on the epicycle, which itself rotates.
Correction: The epicycle is a sphere that carries the planet; the planet is not moving along the epicycle but is fixed on it.

Checkpoint
At which points does the epicycle touch the eccentric?
A) At the apex (ذروة) and perigee (حضيض)
B) At the center and the surface
C) At the equator and the poles
D) At random points

Key Takeaway
The epicycle is a solid sphere that touches the eccentric at the apex and perigee, and carries the planet fixed on it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage stresses that the epicycle is considered solid with no concavity. In your own heart, are there areas where you have allowed 'hollowness'—empty pretense or hypocrisy—where Allah demands solid, sincere faith? What would it take to make that part of your life solid again?
?
Taftazani gives a precise definition of the epicycle. Are there doctrines of your faith that you have accepted in a vague or fuzzy way rather than learning their exact, scripturally based definitions? Commit to learning one such doctrine precisely this week.
?
The epicycle touches the eccentric at only two points: the apex and perigee. In your relationship with Allah, do you only touch the 'heights' and 'depths' of worship when convenient, or is your devotion embedded like the sphere itself, constant and solid within the larger structure of your life? What change is needed to make your worship more continuous?

Roles of Carrier, Director, and Representative
Al-Taftazani explains the roles of carrier, director, and representative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the functions of the carrier, director, and representative spheres, and how they relate to Mercury's complex model.

Core Idea
The carrier holds the epicycle; the director and representative are nested eccentrics.

Having defined the epicycle, al-Taftazani explains the roles of different spheres: the carrier (al-hamil), director (al-mudir), and representative (al-mumaththil). This lesson clarifies these terms and their relationships using Mercury as an example.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on terminology
Read the Arabic passage that explains the inclined sphere, carrier, director, and representative. Pay attention to how each is defined relative to the others.
The passage begins with 'فقوله، ثم في ثخن المائل'.
2
Understand the carrier (ال حامل)
The carrier is the eccentric that contains an epicycle. It 'carries' the center of the epicycle.
3
Understand the director (المدير)
The director is an eccentric that is separate from the carrier, and its center is directed by the carrier.
The relationship is hierarchical: representative → director → carrier.
4
Examine Mercury's special structure
Mercury has an eccentric with two apogees, two perigees, and four complementing bodies. This indicates a more complex layering.
The text mentions 'خارجاً مركز وأوجان، وحضيضان وأربع متممات'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يكون الخارج المركز في ثخن خارج مركز آخر كما في عطارد ومنها التداوير، والتدوير كرة في ثخن الخارج المركز، يماس سطحها محدب الخارج بنقطة يسمى الذروة ومقعره بنقطة مقابلة لها تسمى الحضيض، والكوكب مركوز فيهما بحيث يتماس سطحاهما على نقطة ولم يعتبر لها ولا للكوكب تقعير بل اعتبرا مصمتين فقوله، ثم في ثخن المائل إشارة إلى أن الموافق المركز المشتمل على الخارج المركز هو في القمر المائل، وفي البواقي ممثلاتها، وأن الحامل اسم للخارج المركز إذا كان في ثخنه التدوير لحمله مركز التدوير، وإن خارج المركز مديراً لإدارته مركز الحامل، وهو الخارج المركز الذي ينفصل عن المدير انفصال المدير عن الممثل، ويكون فيه التدوير لعطارد خارجاً مركز وأوجان، وحضيضان وأربع متممات والمائل في المتحيرة اسم للخارج المركز الحامل للتدوير إذا تقرر هذا فنقول للشمس ممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز في ثخنه الشمس، وللقمر ممثل في جوفه مائل في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه القمر ولعطارد وممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز يسمى مديراً في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه عطارد، ولكل من الأربع الباقية ممثل في ثخنه خارج مركز هو الحامل للتدوير فيه الكوكب.
And the eccentric may be in the thickness of another eccentric, as in Mercury. And from these are the epicycles (al-tadawir). And the epicycle is a sphere in the thickness of the eccentric; its surface touches the convex of the eccentric at a point called the apex (al-dharwa) and its concave at an opposite point called the perigee (al-hadid). And the planet is fixed in both such that their two surfaces touch at a point, and concavity is not considered for them nor for the planet, but they are considered solid. So his statement: 'then in the thickness of the inclined [sphere]' indicates that the concentric containing the eccentric is in the inclined [sphere] of the moon, and in the rest, their representatives (mumaththilat). And that 'al-hamil' (the carrier) is the name for the eccentric if there is in its thickness an epicycle, because it carries the center of the epicycle. And that the eccentric is a 'mudir' (director) because its center is directed by the carrier. And it is the eccentric that is separate from the director as the director is separate from the representative. And in it, the epicycle for Mercury has an eccentric and two apogees and two perigees and four complementing bodies. And 'al-mail' (the inclined) in the wandering planets is the name for the eccentric that carries the epicycle. If this is established, then we say: For the Sun, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric in whose thickness is the Sun. For the Moon, there is a representative in its interior an inclined [sphere] in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is the Moon. For Mercury, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric called a director (mudir) in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is Mercury. And for each of the remaining four, there is a representative in whose thickness is an eccentric which is the carrier of the epicycle in which is the planet.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage continues the astronomical discussion by introducing the epicycle (التدوير) and detailing the models for each planet. It begins by noting that an eccentric can be nested within another eccentric, as for Mercury. From such configurations come epicycles, defined as a sphere within the thickness of an eccentric, touching it at two points: the apex (الذروة) and the perigee (الحضيض). The planet is fixed on the epicycle such that the surfaces touch at a point, and both the epicycle and planet are considered solid (not hollow). The text then explains terminology: the 'carrier' (الحامل) is the eccentric that contains an epicycle; the 'director' (المدير) is an eccentric that is separate from the carrier; the 'representative' (الممثل) is a sphere that contains these. For the Moon, the concentric containing the eccentric is in an inclined sphere; for other planets, they have representatives. Mercury's model has an eccentric, two apogees, two perigees, and four complementing bodies. The 'inclined' (المائل) in the wandering planets is the eccentric that carries the epicycle. Finally, it summarizes each planet: Sun has a representative with an eccentric containing the Sun; Moon has a representative with an inclined sphere containing an eccentric carrier; Mercury has a representative with an eccentric director containing an eccentric carrier; the other four planets each have a representative with an eccentric carrier. This establishes the complex layering of spheres used to explain planetary motions.

Key Terms
الحامل
المدير
الممثل
المائل
عطارد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the carrier is the same as the eccentric; actually it is a specific eccentric containing an epicycle.
Correction: Not every eccentric is a carrier; only those that have an epicycle in their thickness.

Checkpoint
What is the 'carrier' (al-hamil) according to the passage?
A) The eccentric that contains an epicycle
B) The concentric sphere
C) The planet itself
D) The inclined sphere

Key Takeaway
The carrier is the eccentric holding the epicycle; the director and representative are higher-level spheres in the nesting.

Planetary Models: Sun, Moon, Mercury, and the Four Wanderers
Al-Taftazani describes the models for each planet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the specific sphere arrangements for the Sun, Moon, Mercury, and the other four planets.

Core Idea
Each planet has a unique nesting of spheres to explain its motion.

Al-Taftazani concludes by summarizing the models for each planet. From the Sun's simple representative-eccentric to Mercury's double eccentric, this lesson provides a clear overview of the Ptolemaic system's complexity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on planetary models
Read the final part of the passage that describes the models for Sun, Moon, Mercury, and the remaining four planets.
It starts with 'والمائل في المتحيرة اسم للخارج المركز الحامل للتدوير'.
2
Understand the inclined sphere for wandering planets
The 'inclined' (المائل) in wandering planets is the eccentric that carries the epicycle. Note that this term is used for the orbiting planets.
The wandering planets are those that move independently of the fixed stars.
3
Identify the model for each planet
List the models: Sun (representative + eccentric), Moon (representative + inclined + eccentric carrier), Mercury (representative + director + eccentric carrier), others (representative + eccentric carrier).
Mercury's model is more complex with an additional director.

?

?

?

When you learn about models that later proved incomplete, does that challenge your reliance on other 'certain' knowledge in matters of faith? How can you hold firm to foundational truths while remaining humble about secondary matters? Ask Allah to guide you to what is true and to protect you from arrogance in your understanding.

The Zodiac, Equinoxes, Solstices, and Seasons
Al-Taftazani describes the intersecting circles and the division of the zodiac into signs and seasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the ancients conceptualized the zodiac, equinoxes, solstices, and seasons based on intersecting celestial circles.

Core Idea
The zodiac is a division of the ecliptic into twelve equal parts, marking the sun's path and defining seasons.

In this passage, al-Taftazani explains the ancient model of the heavens using intersecting circles to divide the zodiac. This system provided the framework for tracking the sun's annual motion and defining the seasons. Understanding this cosmology is key to grasping how medieval scholars interpreted celestial phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the technical terms for circles and points.
The passage is dense with astronomical terminology.
2
Identify the six circles
The text mentions six circles intersecting at the poles of the zodiac. One circle passes through the two intersection points of the celestial equator and ecliptic. Understand that these circles divide the sphere.
3
Understand the division into signs
The circles cut the sphere into twelve equal sections called signs. Each sign is subdivided into degrees, minutes, and seconds. This is the basis of the zodiac.
Note: These signs are not the constellations but mathematical divisions of the ecliptic.
4
Locate the equinoxes and solstices
The two intersection points of the equator and ecliptic are the vernal and autumnal equinoxes. The midpoints between them are the summer and winter solstices. See how these points relate to the sun's motion.
5
Map the signs to seasons
The passage assigns each season a set of zodiac signs. Northern signs (Aries, Taurus, Gemini) are spring; Cancer, Libra, Leo, Virgo are summer; southern signs (Scorpio, Sagittarius) are autumn; Capricorn, Aquarius, Pisces are winter. Note the asymmetry in count per season.
The text lists four signs for summer, which may be an error or variant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثالث: توهمهم الدوائر المتقاطعة على قطبي البرج. قال (المبحث الثالث) توهموا ست دوائر متقاطعة على قطبي البرج قاطعاً لمنطقتها على أبعاد سواء مارة إحداها بنقطتي تقاطع المعدل، ومنطقة البروج، ثم فرضوها قاطعة للعالم، فانقسم الفلك الأعظم وسائر الممثلات أيضاً، اثني عشر قسماً، سموا كل قسم برجاً، وجعلوا كل برج ثلاثين درجة، وكل درجة ستين دقيقة، وكل دقيقة ستين ثانية، وهكذا، وسموا نقطة التقاطع التي تجاوزها الشمس إلى شمال المعدل، اعتدالاً ربيعياً، وإلى جنوبه اعتدالاً خريفياً، ومنتصف ما بين نقطتي التقاطع في الشمال انقلاباً صيفياً، وفي الجنوب انقلاباً شتوياً، وزمان قطع الشمس من البروج الشمالية الحمل، والثور، والجوزاء، ربيعاً، والسرطان والميزان والأسد والسنبلة صيفاً، ومن الجنوب العقرب والقوس خريفاً، والجدي والدلو والحوت شتاءً.
The third investigation: Their imagining the circles intersecting at the poles of the zodiac. He said (the third investigation): They imagined six circles intersecting at the poles of the zodiac, cutting its region at equal distances, one of them passing through the two points of intersection of the equinoctial and the ecliptic. Then they assumed them cutting the universe. So the greatest sphere and all the representatives also divided into twelve sections. They called each section a sign (burj), and made each sign thirty degrees, each degree sixty minutes, each minute sixty seconds, and so on. And they called the point of intersection which the sun crosses to the north of the equinoctial the vernal equinox, and to the south of it the autumnal equinox; and the midpoint between the two points of intersection in the north the summer solstice, and in the south the winter solstice. And the time of the sun's crossing from the northern signs: Aries, Taurus, Gemini, spring; Cancer, Libra, Leo, Virgo, summer; and from the southern: Scorpio, Sagittarius, autumn; Capricorn, Aquarius, Pisces, winter.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is the third investigation (المبحث الثالث) and explains how the ancients imagined circles intersecting at the poles of the zodiac (البرج). They posited six circles that cut the region of the zodiac at equal distances, with one circle passing through the two intersection points of the celestial equator (المعدل) and the ecliptic (منطقة البروج). These circles were assumed to cut the universe, dividing the outermost sphere and all the representative spheres into twelve equal sections, each called a sign (برج). Each sign is 30 degrees, each degree 60 minutes, each minute 60 seconds. The two intersection points of the equator and ecliptic are named: the point where the sun crosses to the north is the vernal equinox (الاعتدال الربيعي), and to the south the autumnal equinox (الاعتدال الخريفي). The midpoints between these two intersections are the summer solstice (الانقلاب الصيفي) in the north and winter solstice (الانقلاب الشتوي) in the south. Finally, the passage lists the zodiac signs associated with each season: northern signs (Aries, Taurus, Gemini) are spring; Cancer, Libra, Leo, Virgo are summer; southern signs (Scorpio, Sagittarius) are autumn; Capricorn, Aquarius, Pisces are winter. Note that the text lists four signs for summer, which may be a variant or error in the source.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The zodiac signs are the constellations themselves.
Correction: Here, the signs are mathematical divisions of the ecliptic (the sun's path), not the constellations. They are used for measuring solar motion and defining seasons.

Checkpoint
What are the two points where the celestial equator and ecliptic intersect called?
A) Equinoxes
B) Solstices
C) Apogee and perigee
D) Apex and perigee

Key Takeaway
The zodiac is a division of the sun's path through the sky, not the constellations, and it forms the basis for defining equinoxes, solstices, and seasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The ancients divided the sky into precise degrees and minutes. Are you more focused on these worldly calculations than on the signs of your Lord in the creation? Where does your heart rest — in the precision of science or in the awe of the Creator?
?
Al-Taftazani explains the solar cycle and seasons as a system imagined by philosophers. Do you ever forget that these cycles are decreed by Allah and not independent? Is your understanding of the seasons merely naturalistic, or does it lead you to gratitude to Allah?
?
The passage describes the zodiac signs as divisions of the sun's path, not constellations with power. Do you ever subtly attribute power to time, fate, or stars in your heart? Where do you place your trust?
